+Jamison Brereton

162
Praise of a Horse (As╠Бvastuti)
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
22 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 3, 6
The first of the two A┼Ыvamedha hymns focuses on the actual sacrifice, with an almost cinematic treatment of the proceedings and an unflinching look at the gory details. The hymn begins with the parading of the horse on the day of sacrifice: the year-long preliminaries in the classical A┼Ыvamedha are not mentioned here, and it is not easy to tell how much elaboration accreted to this ritual in the post-R╠еgvedic periodтАФthough it seems likely that the R╠еgvedic version was a much simpler affair.
After an initial verse calling on an array of gods to bear witness to the celebra tion of the horse, there follow three verses (2тАУ4) devoted to the goat that is led in front of the horse and that is itself sacrificed before the killing of the horse. The goat is the only sacrificial animal mentioned in the hymn besides the horse, in contrast to the classical version of the rite in which a multitude of wild and domestic animals are, at least theoretically, bound for sacrifice (and in general then released). In verses 5тАУ6 a variety of priests (5) and minor ritual functionaries (6; see also the cooks in vs. 12) are mentionedтАФthe priests being urged, somewhat shockingly, to тАЬfill your belliesтАЭ on the sacrifice. This group of officiants seems to correspond on the human level to the gods assembled in verse 1, and all are thus implicated in the performance of the sacrifice, as are the poet himself and his fel
low seers in verse 7.
The gaze then turns to the sacrifice proper (vss. 8тАУ17) and to the equipment asso ciated with the horse (vss. 8, 14, 16), the equipment for cooking the oblation (vs. 13), and, most dramatically, the physical evidence of the slaughter: the fly-blown flesh and the sticky blood and guts (vs. 9), the bloated belly and the smell of the butchered animal (vs. 10), the cooking juices running off the skewered beast on344 I.162
the fire (vs. 11). All of the mentioned paraphernalia and the gore are meant to accompany the horse itself to the gods. This section of the hymn gains much of its power from a dual focus: the gritty reality of an actual sacrifice competes with the reverential attitude to the victim, regularly addressed in the 2nd personтАФsuch that the horse is endowed almost with personhood while at the same time being dismem
bered, cooked, and consumed. For this reason, in 3rd-person contexts we use the pronouns тАЬhe, him, hisтАЭ for the horse, rather than тАЬit,тАЭ et cetera: the poet will not allow us to objectify or neuter-ize the animal and requires us to come to terms with what тАЬweтАЭ are doing to тАЬhim.тАЭ
The description of the dismembering becomes more detailed beginning in verse 18, where the axe approaches the horseтАЩs ribs. Although this carving up logically precedes some of the sacrificial actions treated beforeтАФespecially the cooking of the already butchered horseтАФthere is a reason for its positioning here. We are entering the third and last part of the hymn, in which the horse is sent on his journey to the gods. The emphasis in these carving verses (18тАУ20) is on the proper order of the cut
ting and the patterned positioning of the pieces of the horse, so that he can make its own way on his тАЬundamagedтАЭ legs (vss. 18, 20). The pieces of the horse are arranged to re-form the actual body of the horse, and this reconstituted body is complemented by the lifebreath (─Бtman) that is also making the journey to the gods (vs. 20). The climax is reached in verse 21, where the horse is assured that he is not dead or injured and that his journey to the gods will be made easily, in company with the mounts of the gods. The hymn ends (vs. 22) with the hope that the sacrificed horse will bring us good things, and with an unemphatic prayer for our тАЬguiltlessness,тАЭ presumably because of the potential guilt associated with the killing of the horse.
To those who know the classical ┼Ыrauta version of the A┼Ыvamedha the most strik ing omission in this hymn is any mention of the sexual intercourse (or simulated inter course) of the chief wife of the king and sacrificer with the just slaughtered horse. If our interpretation of X.86, the Vr╠ес╣г─Бkapi hymn, is correctтАФthat it is a burlesqued ver sion of an A┼Ыvamedha with a randy monkey as victimтАФthe missing sexual element in our hymn here was omitted out of delicacy rather than being unknown to the R╠еgveda.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet neither Mitra nor Varuс╣Зa, Aryaman, ─Аyu, Indra, с╣Ъbhukс╣гin,nor the Maruts, censure us; when we proclaim in the sacrifice the virtus of the swift horse sprung from the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

─Аyu = v─Бyu (─Бyuс╕е satatagant─Б v─Бyuс╕е, vak─Бralopo v─Б);

с╣Ъbhukс╣гin = Indra; but,here Praj─Бpati, he in whom the с╣Ыbhus,or the devas, abide (kс╣гiyanti); sprung from the gods: devaja-tasya = born as the type of various divinities, who are identified with different parts (e.g. uс╣г─Б v─Б a┼Ыvasya medhyasya ┼Ыiraс╕е: Bс╣Ыhad─Бraс╣Зyaka Upaniс╣гad 1.1.1);

Legend: the horse’s origin from the sun, either direct, or through the agency of the Vasus: sur─Бd a┼Ыvam vasavo nirataс╣гс╣нa

+Jamison Brereton

Let not Mitra, Varuс╣Зa, Aryaman, ─Аyu, Indra the lord of the R╠еbhus, and the Maruts disregard us
when we shall proclaim the heroic deeds of the prizewinning, god-born racehorse at the ritual distribution.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

Although the collection of gods serving as witnesses in ab seems somewhat random, the same set recurs in V.41.2, as Geldner points out. The reason for their association there is no clearer than here.

P─Бda d, pravakс╣гy─Б╠Бmaс╕е (vidath├й) v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi, is a variant on the famous opening of I.32, the great Indra hymn, ├нndrasya n├║ v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi pr├бvocam. The gen. ├нndrasya of I.32.1 is matched by the long gen. phrase in our c: (y├бd) v─Бj├нno dev├бj─Бtasya s├бpteс╕е тАЬof the prize-winning, god-born race-horse.тАЭ For another variant on this phrase in D─лrghatamasтАЩs oeuvre, see I.154.1. It is striking here that v─лry─Б╠Ас╣Зi тАШheroic/manlyтАЩ deeds are attributed to a horse; the establishment of тАЬpersonhoodтАЭ for the horse, discussed in the published introduction, begins here in the very first verse.

+Griffith

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen they, (the priests), bring the prepared offering to the presence (of the horse), who has been bathed and decorated with rich (trappings), the various-coloured goat going before him, bleating, becomes an acceptable offering to Indra and P┼лс╣гan.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The prepared offering: r─Бtim-gс╣Ыbh─лt─Бm = lit. the seized wealth; the offering to be made for the horse;

P┼лс╣гan = Agni; the goat is to be tied to the front of the horse at the sacrificial post, such a goat, black-necked, kс╣Ыс╣гnagr─лva (─Бgneyaс╕е kс╣Ыс╣гс╣Зagr─лvaс╕е: Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 5.5.22), being always regarded as an ─Бgneya pa┼Ыu, or victim sacred to Agni, and to be offered to him (K─Бty─Бyana S┼лtra 98). A black goat is also dedicated to p┼лс╣гan, along with soma (Yajus. xxix.58; but, he is also to be attached to the n─Бbhi or middle of the horse (Yajus. xxiv.1)

+Jamison Brereton

When they lead the gift [=goat] held fast in front of (the horse, which is) decked out with a fresh garment and with family treasure,
facing well forward, constantly bleating, the goat, representing all forms, passes into the fold of Indra and P┼лс╣гan.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It may not be clear in the published translation that it is the horse that is bedecked (pr─Б╠Бvс╣Ыtasya), not the goat.

vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa- modifying the goat in c is taken by most as a bland color term (Geldner/Witzel Got┼Н тАШallfarbigтАЩ, Doniger тАШdappledтАЩ), but, esp. because in the next vs. (3b) the goat is called vi┼Ыv├бdevya-, I think the qualifier is meant to convey more meaning: perhaps to indicate that the goat stands for all the other animals (which, as disc. in the published introduction, are literally tied up for sacrifice in the later versions of the A┼Ыvamedha), hence my тАЬrepresenting all forms.тАЭ

+Griffith

What time they bear before the Courser, covered with trappings and with wealth, the grasped oblation,
The dappled goat goeth straightforward, bleating, to the place dear to Indra and to Pusan.

+Geldner

Wenn sie vor dem mit Gewand und Erbst├╝cken bedeckten, die Opfergabe, gefa├Яt, voraus f├╝hren, so geht der allfarbige Bock meckernd, willig voran zu Indra┬┤s und Pusan┬┤s lieber Zuflucht.

+Grassmann

Wenn sie die ergriffene Spende des mit Reichthum und Schmuck bedeckten [Rosses] am Zaume f├╝hren, so geht sch├╢n vorangef├╝hrt der bunte Ziegenbock meckernd hin zu dem lieben Sitze des Indra und Puschan.

+Elizarenkova

рдПрд╖рдГ рдЫрд╛рдЧрдГ рд╢реГрдЩреНрдЧрд░рд╣рд┐рддреЛрд╜рдЬрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЗрди рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирд╛ рд╢реАрдШреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЗрдирд╛рд╢реНрд╡реЗрди рд╕рд╣ рдкреВрд╖реНрдгрдГ рдкреЛрд╖рдХрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рднрд╛рдЧрдГ рднрдЬрдиреАрдпрдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд░реНрд╣рдГ ред рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рд╛рддреНрдордХрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рддрджрд░реНрд╣рддреНрд╡реЗрди рд╕рд░реНрд╡рджреЗрд╡рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдПрд╡рдВрд╡рд┐рдзрдГ рдЕрдЬрдГ рдкреБрд░рдГ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рддреН рдиреАрдпрддреЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрддреН рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдПрд╡рдВ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрддреЗ рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд┐рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░реАрдгрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреБрд░реЛрдбрд╛рд╢рдВ рдкреБрд░рд╕реНрддрд╛рджреНрджрд╛рддрд╡реНрдпрдореН рдПрдирдореН рдЕрдЬрдВ рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдпреЛрддреНрдкрд╛рджрдХреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдГред тАШрддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯрд╛ рд░реВрдкрд╛рдгрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐’ ( рддреИ. рд╕рдВ. рез. рел. реп.реи) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ ред рддреВрд░реНрдгрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкрдХреЛрд╜рдЧреНрдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛ред тАШрдЙрднреЗ рддреНрд╡рд╖реНрдЯреБрд░реНрдмрд┐рднреНрдпрддреБрдГ ’ (рдЛ. рд╕рдВ. рез. репрел.рел) рдЗрддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ’ рдЕрд╣реЛрд░рд╛рддреНрд░реЗ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛рд░рдгреА рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд╛ ’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рео. резрел) рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХреЗрди рдЕрд░рдгреА рдмрд┐рднреНрдпрддреБрд░рд┐рддреНрдпреБрдХреНрддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрд░рдгрд┐рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реЗрд╡реЗрддрд┐ рдЧрдореНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрд╛ рдЕрд░рдгрд╡рддрд╛ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЗрди рд╕рд╣ рд╕реМрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕рд╛рдп рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирд╛рдиреНрдирдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддрдореН рдЕрднрд┐ рдЬрд┐рдиреНрд╡рддрд┐ рдкреНрд░реАрддрд┐рд╣реЗрддреБрдХрдВ рдХрд░реЛрддрд┐ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThis goat, the portion of Pu+с╣гan fit for all the gods, is brought first with the fleet courser, to that Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б may prepare him along with the horse, as an acceptable preliminary offering for the (sacrificial) food.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The portion of P┼лс╣гan: he is to be offered in sacrifice to P┼лс╣гan or Agni;

Tvaс╣гс╣н─Б = sarvasyotp─Бdaka, the producer of all forms; tvaс╣гс╣н─Б r┼лp─Бс╣Зi vikaroti (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 1.5.92); or, identified wiith Agni;preliminary offering puroс╕Н─Б┼Ыam = offering of cakes and butter; purast─Бd-d─Бtavyam, that which is to be first offered

+Jamison Brereton

This billy-goat, belonging to all the gods, is led in front, along with the prizewinning horse, as P┼лс╣гanтАЩs portion.
When (they lead the goat) as the pleasing fore-offering along with the steed, it is Tvaс╣гс╣нar himself who stimulates him for (the deed) that
brings good fame.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

It is appropriate that the goat, if it тАЬrepresents all formsтАЭ (see disc. of the previous vs.), should belong to all the gods. That it should also be тАЬP┼лс╣гanтАЩs portionтАЭ (p┼лс╣гс╣З├│ bh─Бg├бс╕е, 3b and 4c) probably follows from the fact that P┼лс╣гan тАЬhas goats for horsesтАЭ (aj─Б╠Б┼Ыva-: 5x, always of P┼лс╣гan) and is generally associated with goats.

As for Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs involvement, Geldner (sim. Witzel Got┼Н) simply says that Tvaс╣гс╣нar is the creator esp. of animals, but I think there is a tighter connection. Tvaс╣гс╣нar is a required presence in the ─Аpr─л hymns, the litanies that accompany the animal sacrifice. The verse devoted to him in each hymn occurs immediately before the тАЬLord of the Forest,тАЭ namely the stake to which the sacrificial animal is tied, releases the animal for sacrifice. Just before that, Tvaс╣гс╣нar both produces life (e.g., II.3.9, III.4.9-VII.2.9) and assists at the sacrifice (V.5.9), escorting the sacrificial animal to the gods (X.70.9) or at least pointing the way (II.3.9). Most strikingly Tvaс╣гс╣нar is once called vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa- (I.13.10) and several times enacts that epithet dramatically: I.188.9 tv├бс╣гс╣н─Б r┼лp─Б╠Бс╣Зi h├н prabh├║с╕е pa┼Ы┼л╠Бn v├н┼Ыv─Бn sam─Бnaj├й тАЬBecause preeminent Tvaс╣гс╣нar anointed all the beasts (with) their formsтАЭ; X.110.9 r┼лpa├нr ├бpiс╣Г┼Ыad bh├║van─Бni v├н┼Ыv─Б тАЬhe adorned all the creatures with their forms.тАЭ In our verse Tvaс╣гс╣нar stimulates/quickens the goat immediately before its sacrifice and indeed for its sacrifice, and that goat has just been characterized as vi┼Ыv├бr┼лpa-. Thus Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs constant appearance in the ─Аpr─л hymns shows that this god has a defined role in the animal sacrifice, and that role, somewhat paradoxically, involves both giving life and setting the stage for taking it away by sacrifice. This is less of a paradox in the conceptual context of the animal sacrifice: as noted in the published introduction, a good deal of this hymn is devoted to reconstituting the sacrificed horse and endowing it with life-breath. Tvaс╣гс╣нar thus has a role in both, and we see it here first in connection with the goat that represents all creatures. Tvaс╣гс╣нar recurs in vs. 19 below.

+Griffith

Dear to all Gods, this goat, the share of Pusan, is first led forward with the vigorous Courser,
While Tvastar sends him forward with the Charger, acceptable for sacrifice, to glory.

+Geldner

Dieser Ziegenbock, f├╝r alle G├╢tter bestimmt, wird mit dem siegesgewohnten Ro├Я vorausgef├╝hrt als Anteil des Pusan. Wenn sie den Bock als willkommnes Voropfer mit dem Rennpferd f├╝hren, so ermuntert ihn Tvastri zu r├╝hmlichem Werke.

+Grassmann

Dieser Bock wird dem schnellen Rosse vorangef├╝hrt als Antheil des Puschan, der allen G├╢ttern willkommen, wenn er den erfreuenden Opferkuchen zu gleich mit dem Renner empfangen hat, so bef├╢rdert ihn Tvaschtar zu hohem Ruhme.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhen the priests at the season (of the ceremony), lead forth the horse, the offering devoted to the gods, thrice round (the sacrificial fire); then the goat, the portion of P┼лс╣гan, goes first, announcing the sacrificer to the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The goat is to be first immolated

+Jamison Brereton

When the sons of Manu lead around the horse to be offered three times along (the path) that goes to the gods in proper order,
then the goat, P┼лс╣гanтАЩs portion, goes first, announcing the sacrifice to the gods.

+Griffith

When thrice the men lead round the Steed, in order, who goeth to the Gods as meet oblation,
The goat precedeth him, the share of Pusan, and to the Gods the sacrifice announceth.

+Geldner

Wenn die Menschen das zum Opfer bestimmte Ro├Я dreimal der Reihe nach den G├╢tterweg herumf├╝hren, so geht dabei der Opferanteil des Pusan voran, der Bock, der den G├╢ttern das Opfer meldet.

+Grassmann

Wenn die Menschen das mit Opfertrank versehene zu den G├╢ttern gehende Ross nach dem Brauche dreimal herumf├╝hren, so geht der Ziegenbock als erster Antheil des Puschan, den G├╢ttern das Opfer ank├╝ndigend.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe invoker of the gods, the minister of the rite, the offerer of the oblation, the kindler of the fire, the bruiser of the Soma, the director of the ceremony, the saage (superintendent of the whole); do you replenish the rivers by this well-ordered, well-conducted, sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The invoker of the gods: designations applied to eight of the sixteen priests employed at a solemn rite: the two first are: hot─Б and adhvaryu;

Avay─Бj = pratiprasth─Бt─Б, who brings and plural ces the offering;

Agnimindha = agn─лdh, the kindler of the fire;

Gr─Бvagr─Бbha = the praiser of the stones that bruise the Soma,or he who applies the stones to that purpose;

┼Ъaс╣Гst─Б = pra┼Ы─Бst─Б;

Suvipra = Brahm─Б (brahmaiko j─Бte j─Бte vidy─Бm vadatibrahm─Б sarvavidyaс╕е sarva veditumarhati: Nirukta 1.8); replenish the rivers: vakс╣гaс╣З─Б apс╣Ыс╣Зadhvam, nad─лс╕е p┼лrayata, fill the rivers; the consequence of sacrifice being rain and fertility; or, it may mean, offer rivers of butter, milk, curds, and the like

+Jamison Brereton

The Hotar, the Adhvaryu, the Expiator [?], the Fire-kindler, the Handler of the Pressing-stones, and the well-inspired ReciterтАФ
with this sacrifice, well prepared and well offered, fill your bellies.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of priests contains the hapax ─Б╠Бvay─Б(с╕е), whose derivation and meaning are unclear. For suggestions and disc. see, e.g., Oldenberg, Geldner, Renou I tentatively favor a connection with ├бva тИЪy─Б тАШpropitiate, expiateтАЩ, but the form presents grave difficulties for that analysis. For one thing, we should expect a root-noun cmpd.

(*)avay─Б╠Б- with short initial vowel and accent on the root – and in fact we get just that form in I.173.12. See detailed disc. by Scarlatta (404-7, with our form treated in n. 565).

However, it can be pointed out that this lexeme is mutilated elsewhere – e.g., in nearby I.165.15 (but Agastya, not D─лrghatamas), where vay─Б╠Бm is better read тАШvay─Б╠Бm (i.e., avay─Б╠Бm), which sandhi form its position after tanv├и would allow. Thus, the connection with ├бva тИЪy─Б reflected in the published translation is quite insecure, and it may be best to follow Oldenberg in accepting the traditional analysis as ─Б╠Б-vayas-, rendering it тАШwhose life force is (right) hereтАЩ. This avoids the formal difficulties, but I donтАЩt see what kind of priest this would be.

There is a mild disconnect between the two hemistichs: the first half is a list entirely in the nominative, but the second contains a 2nd pl. impv. ─Б╠Бpс╣Ыс╣Зadhvam, whose 2nd ps. subjects should be the nominatives of ab.

+Griffith

Invoker, ministering priest, atoner, fire-kindler Soma-presser, sage, reciter,
With this well ordered sacrifice, well finished, do ye fill full the channels of the rivers.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhether they be those who cut the (sacrificial) post, or those who bear the post, or those who fasten the rings on the top of the post, to which the horse (is bound); or those who prepare the vessels in which the food of the horse is dressed; let the exertions of them all fulfil our expectation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The post: twenty-one posts, of different kinds of wood, each twenty-one cubits long, are to be set up, to which the different animals are to be fastened, amounting to three hundred and forty-nine, besides two hundred and sixty wild animals, making a total of six hundred and nine (K─Бty─Бyana); the text seems to refer to a single post: caс╣г─Бlam ye a┼Ыvay┼лp─Бya takс╣гati: caс╣г─Бla = a wooden ring, or bracelet, on the top of the sacrificial post; or, it was perhaps a metal ring at the foot of the post

+Jamison Brereton

The hewers of the sacrificial post and its conveyors, those who
fashion the knob for the post for the horse,
and those who assemble the equipment for cooking the steedтАФlet the applause also of those urge us on.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The list of personnel involved in the sacrifice here includes some apparently marginal and humble roles, perhaps to implicate the largest possible group in the potential blood-guilt of the sacrifice.

I render the ut├│ in d with тАШalsoтАЩ; this is also KleinтАЩs tr., though his disc. of the passage seems to seek a straight conjunctive role (DGRV I.448-49). See the same expression in 12d.

+Griffith

The hewers of the post and those who carry it, and those who carve the knob to deck the Horse’s stake;
Those who prepare the cooking-vessels for the Steed,–may the approving help of these promote our work.

+Geldner

Die Pfostenhauer und Pfostentr├дger und die den Knauf f├╝r den Rosspfosten zimmern, und die f├╝r das Rennpferd das Kochger├дt zusammentragen, auch deren Beifall soll uns f├╢rdern.

+Grassmann

Die den Pfosten bebauen und die ihn herbeifahren, die den Knauf f├╝r den Pferdepfosten zimmern, und die f├╝r den Renner das Kochgeschirr zusammenbringen, auch deren freundliche H├╝lfe fordere uns.

рдордиреНрдо рдордирдиреАрдпрдВ рдлрд▓рдВ рд╕реБрдорддреН рдЙрдк рдкреНрд░рд╛рдЧрд╛рддреН рдЙрдкрдкреНрд░реИрддреБ ред тАШрд╕реБрдорддреНрд╕реНрд╡рдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ’ ( рдирд┐рд░реБ. рем.реиреи ) рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрд╛рд╕реНрдХрдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рд╕реНрд╡рдпрдореЗрд╡ рдорд╛рджрдпрд┐рддреГрддрдореЗ рдордпрд┐ рдЕрдзрд╛рдпрд┐ рдзреАрдпрддреЗ ред рдлрд▓рднреВрддрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдГ рдЖрдЧрддрдГ рд╕ рдЪ рдордпрд╛ рдзреГрддрдГ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрд┐рдорд░реНрдердореН ред рд╡реАрддрдкреГрд╖реНрдардГ рд╕рд╛рдзреБрдкреЛрд╖рдгреЗрди рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрдкрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рджреНрднрд╛рдЧрдГ рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрдкреГрд╖реНрдареЛ рд╡рд╛ ред рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рджреГрдкреНрддрдГ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢реЛрд╜рдпрдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдорд╛рд╢рд╛рдГ рдкреВрд░рдпрд┐рддреБрдореН рдЙрдк рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рдпрд╛рдЧрд╛рд░реНрдердорд╛рдЧрддрдореН рдПрдирдВ рд╕реБрдмрдиреНрдзреБрдВ рд╢реЛрднрдирдмрдиреНрдзрдирдорд╢реНрд╡рдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЖрд╢рд╛рд╕реНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреБрд╖реНрдЯреЗ рдкреЛрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдЪрдХреГрдо рдХреБрд░реНрдордГ ред рддрдВ рдЪ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдГ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рди рдЛрддреНрд╡рд┐рдЬрдГ рдЛрд╖рдпрдГ рдЕрддреАрдиреНрджреНрд░рд┐рдпрджреНрд░рд╖реНрдЯрд╛рд░реЛрд╜рдиреНрдпреЗ рд╡рд╛ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛ рдЛрд╖рдпрд╢реНрдЪ рдЕрдиреБ рдорджрдиреНрддрд┐ рдЕрдиреБрдореЛрджрдиреНрддрд╛рдореН ред рд╕рдореНрдпрдХреН рдХреГрддрдорд┐рддрд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рддреБрд╖реНрдпрдиреНрддреБ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay my desire be of itself accomplished, such as it has been entertained, that the smooth-backed steed should come to (gratify) the expectations of the gods; we have made him well-secured for the nutriment of the gods; let the wise saints now rejoice.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

(When) he went forth, at that same time my thought was producedтАФ (when) the straight-backed (horse went forth) to the regions of
the gods.
The inspired seers cheer him on. We have made him well connected to the prospering of the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I analyse pr─Б╠Бg─Бt as pra-├бg─Бt, rather than Pp. pr├б ag─Бt – in other words with an accented verb, which is in a non overtly marked subordinate clause, with adh─Бyi in the main clause. I then supply the same verb again in b. This may seem over-tricky, but it avoids taking sm├бt тАж m├бnma as a parenthesis and ties together the two ritual actions, the procession of the horse and the production of the poem.

+Griffith

Forth, for the regions of the Gods, the Charger with his smooth back is come my prayer attends him.
In him rejoice the singers and the sages. A good friend have we won for the Gods’ banquet.

+Geldner

Er ist in die Gefilde der G├╢tter eingegangen, der gradr├╝ckige Renner - ein sch├╢nes Gedicht ist von mir gemacht. Die redekundigen Rishi┬┤s jubeln ihm nach. Wir haben ihn zu einem guten Genossen im Gest├╝te der G├╢tter gemacht.

+Grassmann

Das Ross mit glattem R├╝cken ist vorgeschritten, тАУ mein Gebet ist ihm mitgegeben тАУ zu den Oertern der G├╢tter, ihm jauchzen die begeisterten S├дnger nach; wir haben es bei dem Mahle den G├╢ttern verwandt gemacht.

+Elizarenkova

рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдГ рдЧрдордирд╡рддреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдпрддреН рджрд╛рдо рдЧреНрд░реАрд╡рд╛рдмрджреНрдзрд╛ рд░рдЬреНрдЬреБрдГ ред рдпрдЪреНрдЪ рд╕рдВрджрд╛рдирдВ рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧрд╡рдЪреНрдЫреЗрджрдХрдВ рдмрдиреНрдзрдХрдВ рдкрд╛рджрдмрдиреНрдзрдирдВ рджрд╛рдо рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдпрд╛ рдЪ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рдгреНрдпрд╛ рд╢рд┐рд░рд╕рд┐ рдмрджреНрдзрд╛ рдЦрд▓реАрдирд░рдЬреНрдЬреБрдГ рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ рее рд╢рд┐рд░рдГрд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рддреН тАШрднрд╡реЗ рдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐’ рдЗрддрд┐ рдпрддреН ред тАЬ рдпреЗ рдЪ рддрджреНрдзрд┐рддреЗ’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рез. ремрез ) рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реАрд░реНрд╖рдиреНрднрд╛рд╡рдГред рддрд┐рддреНрд╕реНрд╡рд░рд┐рддрдГ рее рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ рдШ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдЖрд╕реНрдпреЗ рдореБрдЦреЗ рдкреНрд░рднреГрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╣реГрддрдВ рдкреНрд░рдХреНрд╖рд┐рдкреНрддрдВ рддреГрдгрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддрд┐ ред рдШрд╢рдмреНрджреЛ рд╣рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рд╕ рдЪ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд┐рджреНрдзреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рддрд╛ рддрд╛рдирд┐ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рдЕрдкрд┐ рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рд╕рдВрдмрдиреНрдзреАрдирд┐ рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╕реНрддреБ рд╕рдиреНрддреБ рджреЗрд╡реЗрд╖реБ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рднрд╡рдиреНрддреБ ред рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд╡рдВ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдиреБрд╡рдиреНрддреБ рд╡рд╛ рее рд╡рдЪрдирд╡реНрдпрддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рдЕрддреНрд░реЛрдкрдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рджреЗрд╡рддреНрд╡рдВ рдХрд┐рд▓ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рддрддреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдГ рди рдЖрд╢рд╛рд╕рдиреАрдпрд╛ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the halter and the heel-ropes of the fleet courser, and the head-ropes, the girths, and any other (part of the harness); and the grass that has been put into his mouth; may all these be with you, (horse), amongst the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The heel-ropes: d─Бma = a rope fastened round the horse’s neck;

Sand─Бna = one that fastens his feet; any other part of the harness: ┼Ыiс╣гaс╣Зy─Б ra┼Ыan─Б rajjuс╕е: ┼Ыirс╣гaс╣Зy─Б = the rope that is fastened to the head, the reins;

Rajjuс╕е = rope

+Jamison Brereton

The lead-rope of the prizewinner, the harness of the steed, the halter on his head and his bridle,
and the grass brought up into his mouthтАФlet all this of yours be also among the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The exact referents of these pieces of horse tackle are not clear.

P─Бda d contains a nice ex. of a neut. pl. subj. with sg. verb.

+Griffith

May the fleet Courser’s halter and his heel-ropes, the head-stall and the girths and cords about him.
And the grass put within his mouth to bait him,–among the Gods, too, let all these be with thee.

+Geldner

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever the flies may eat of the raw flesh of the horse; whatever (grease) is smeared upon the brush or upon the axe; (what is smeared) upon the hands or the nails of the immolator, may all this be with you, (horse), amongst the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Whatever is smeared: svarau svadhitau riptam, or liptam, smeared: the flesh that is smeared;or, unguent with which the animal is anointed;

Svaru = implement used used in anointing; svaruс╣З─Б pa┼Ыum anakti = grease of fat;

Svadhiti = axe; explained elliptically: chedanak─Бle,or avad─Бnak─Бle, at the time of cutting up or dissecting, or, pa┼Ыuchedana-s─Бdhana ─Бs─лс╕е = a sword or knife, the instrumental ument of cutting up the victim; N─лti-ma├▒jari cites a text, in which the sacrificers are vaiс╣гс╣Зavas: dhanyaste vaiс╣гс╣Зav─Б dev─Бn yajante pa┼Ыoram─лс╣гam ┼Ыamiturnakha hastastham deveс╣гс╣нam makс╣гik─Бsitam = happy are the vaiс╣гс╣Зavas, who worship the gods with the consecrated flesh of an animal, adhering to the nails and hands of the immolator, and eaten by flies;

Makс╣гik─Б = pyrites ores

+Jamison Brereton

What of the horseтАЩs flesh a fly has eaten, or what is smeared on the sacrificial post or on the axe,
what is on the hands of the Queller-priest and what on his nailsтАФlet all this of yours be also among the gods.

+Griffith

What part of the Steed’s flesh the fly hath eaten, or is left sticking to the post or hatchet,
Or to the slayer’s hands and nails adhereth,–among the Gods, too, may all this be with thee.

+Geldner

+Grassmann

Was von dem Fleische des Perdes des Fliege frass, oder was an dem Opferpfosten oder am Beile h├дngen geblieben ist, was an den H├дnden, was an den N├дgeln des Schl├дchters, alles das sei dein eigen bei den G├╢ttern.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever undigested grass fall from this belly; whatever particle of raw flesh may remain; let the immolators make the whole free from defect, and so cook the pure (offering) that it may be perfectly dressed.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Particle: gandhan = le┼Ыaс╕е, a little part; may be perfectly dressed: medham ┼Ыс╣Ыtap─Бkam pacantu = let them cook the pure flesh with perfect cooking; i.e. make it fit for the gods, and not done toomuch or toolittle, as may be fit for pitс╣Ыs and men

+Jamison Brereton

The contents of his belly that bloats up, the odor of his raw fleshтАФ let the Queller-priests make that well-done and let them cook the ritual offering until itтАЩs cooked to readiness.

+Griffith

Food undigested steaming from his belly, and any odour of raw flesh remaining,
This let the immolators set in order and dress the sacrifice with perfect cooking.

+Geldner

Der Speiserest in seinem Leib, der ausd├╝nstet, der Geruch seines rohen Fleisches, das alles sollen die Zurichter zurecht machen und sie sollen das Opfertier gar kochen.

+Grassmann

Was die Ged├дrme des Bauches ausd├╝nsten, welches der Duft des rohen Fleisches ist, das m├╢gen die Schl├дchter sch├╢n zurecht bringen, und m├╢gen den Opfertrank gar kochen.

рд╣реЗ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡ рддреЗ рддрд╡ рдЕрдЧреНрдирд┐рдирд╛ рдкрдЪреНрдпрдорд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдЧрд╛рддреНрд░рд╛рддреН рдпрддреН рдКрд╖реНрдорд░реВрдкрдВ рд░рд╕реЛ рд╡рд╛ рдпрддреНрдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рддреН рдЕрд╡рдзрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдирд┐рд╣рддрд╕реНрдп рдирд┐рдГрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рд╣рддрд╕реНрдп рддрд╡ рдпрджрдЩреНрдЧрдВ рд░рд╕рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╢реВрд▓рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖реНрдп рдЕрд╡рдзрд╛рд╡рддрд┐ рдирд┐рд░реНрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ред рддрддреН рддрджрдЩреНрдЧрдВ рднреВрдореНрдпрд╛рдВ рдорд╛ рдЖ рд╢реНрд░рд┐рд╖рддреН рдЖрд╢реНрд▓рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдВ рдорд╛ рднреВрддреН рее рд╢реНрд░рд┐рд╖реЗрдГ рдкреБрд╖рд╛рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдЕрдЩреНрее рдкрд╛рдХрд╕рдордпреЗ рддрдерд╛ рдорд╛ рддреГрдгреЗрд╖реБ рд╡рд┐рд╢рд╕рдирд╕рдордпреЗ рджрд░реНрднреЗрд╖реБ рдорд╛ рдЕрдкрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ ред рддрд░реНрд╣рд┐ рддрддреНрдкрддрд┐рддрдВ рдХреБрддреНрд░ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ рдЪреЗрддреН рдЙрдЪреНрдпрддреЗред рддрддреН рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рдореН рдЙрд╢рджреНрднреНрдпрдГ рдХреГрддреНрд╕реНрдирдВ рд╣рд╡рд┐рдГ рдХрд╛рдордпрдорд╛рдиреЗрднреНрдпрдГ рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпрдГ рд░рд╛рддрдВ рджрддреНрддрдореН рдЕрд╕реНрддреБ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhatever (portion) of your slaughtered (body) fall from your carcass when it is being roasted by the fire, (escaping) from the spit; let it not be left on the ground,nor on the (sacred) grass, but let it (all) be given to the longing gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

G─Бtr─Бd agnin─Б pacyam─Бn─Бd abhi ┼Ы┼лlam:in the preceding hymn, ┼Ыс╣Ыtap─Бkam = boiling; and a ukha, a pot or cauldron is specified in hymn 13 for the same purpose; this use is at variance with the use of ┼Ы┼лla or spit; the inference is that part was boiled and part was roasted; it is suggested that the portion that falls may be the rasa, the dripping, which is to be received upon darbha grass, afterwards probably to be thrown on the fire

+Jamison Brereton

What runs down from your leg as itтАЩs being cooked by the fire when you have been impaled on the spitтАФ
let that not stick to the ground nor to the grasses; let it be given to the gods, who are eager for it.

+Griffith

What from thy body which with fire is roasted, when thou art set upon the spit, distilleth,
Let not that lie on earth or grass neglected, but to the longing Gods let all be offered.

+Geldner

Was von deinem am Feuer gebratenen K├╢rperteil abrinnt, wenn du an den Spie├Я gesteckt bist, das soll nicht auf den Boden, nicht an den Gr├дsern h├дngen bleiben. Den verlangenden G├╢ttern soll das gespendet sein!

+Grassmann

Was aus deinem am Feuer gebratenen Gliede, wenn du an den Bratspiess gesteckt bist, herabtr├дufelt, das m├╢ge nicht auf die Erde fallen, nicht auf die Gr├дser, den begehrenden G├╢ttern m├╢ge es gespendet sein.

+Elizarenkova

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдпреЗ рдкрдХреНрд╡рдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рд╡рдпрд╡рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдкрд░рд┐рддрдГ рдкрд╛рд╡рдирдмреБрджреНрдзреНрдпрд╛ рдИрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреЗ ред рдп рдИрдВ рдпреЗ рдЪреИрдирдВ рд╕реБрд░рднрд┐рдГ рд╢реЛрднрдирдЧрдиреНрдзрдГ рдЕрддрдГ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╣рд░ рдХрд┐рдВрдЪрд┐рджрдкреНрдпрд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджреЗрд╣рд┐ рдЗрддрд┐ рдЖрд╣реБрдГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдирд┐рдГрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдг рджреЗрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ рд╣рд░реЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣реБрдГ ред рдпрддрдГ рд╕реБрд░рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрддреЛ рджреЗрд╡рдпреЛрдЧреНрдпрдорд┐рддрд┐ ред рдХрд┐рдВрдЪ рдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрд╡рддреЛ рдорд╛рдВрд╕рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдореБрдкрд╛рд╕рддреЗ рдпреЗ рдирд░рд╛рдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдп рдЕрд░реНрд╡рддрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╣реБрддрд╢рд┐рд╖реНрдЯрдорд╛рдВрд╕рдпрд╛рдЪрдирд╛рдореБрдкрд╛рд╕рддреЗ рдХрд╛рдВрдХреНрд╖рдиреНрддреЗ ред рдЙрддреЛ рдЕрдкрд┐ рдЪ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЙрдХреНрддрд╡рд┐рдзрд╛рдирд╛рдореН рдЕрднрд┐рдЧреВрд░реНрддрд┐рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рддрдГ рдЙрджреНрдпрдордирдВ рдирдГ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рдиреН рдЗрдиреНрд╡рддреБ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдкреНрдиреЛрддреБ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реЗ рдЙрдкрд╛рд▓рдмреНрдзреЗ рдПрд╡рдВ рд╕реНрдкреГрд╣рдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рддрдерд╛ рдпрдЬреНрдЮреЛ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╛рд╣рдпрддреБ рдЗрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рдордиреНрддреНрд░рдГ рджреЗрд╡рдкрд░реЛ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдЦреНрдпреЗрдпрдГ ред рдпреЗ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рд╡рд╛рдЬрд┐рдирдВ рдкрдХреНрд╡рдВ рдкрд░рд┐рдкрд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддрд┐ рдХрджрд╛ рд╣реЛрд╖реНрдпрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд▓рдореНрдмрдВ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯреНрд╡рд╛ рдпреЗ рдЪ рд╕реБрд░рднрд┐рд░реАрдореЗрдирдВ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╣рд░ рдирд┐рдГрд╢реЗрд╖реЗрдгрд╛рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рджреЗрд╣реАрддреНрдпрд╛рд╣реБрдГ рдпреЗ рдЪрд╛рд░реНрд╡рддреЛрд╜рд╢реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рдорд╛рдВрд╕рднрд┐рдХреНрд╖рд╛рдореБрдкрд╛рд╕рддреЗ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдорднрд┐рдЧреВрд░реНрддрд┐рд░реНрди рдЗрдиреНрд╡рддреБ рддреЗрд╖рд╛рдореН рдЙрджреНрдпрдордГ рд╕рдлрд▓реЛ рднрд╡рддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet their exertions be for our good who watch the cooking of the horse; who say, it is fragrant; therefore give us some; who solicit the flesh of the horse as alms.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Therefore give us some: ya ─лm ─Бhuс╕е suribhir nirhareti = ye cainam ┼Ыobhana gandho ataс╕е ki├▒cid asmabhyam dehi = who say of it, it is fragrant, therefore, give us some; or, give to to the gods;

Nirhara = take off, or give, having no government

+Jamison Brereton

Those who inspect the prizewinner when cooked and who say about him: тАЬIt smells good! Take it off (the fire)!тАЭ
and those who draw near in hopes of a share of the meat of the steedтАФ let the applause also of those urge us on.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

I do not believe that bhikс╣г─Б╠Б- has yet developed the later ubiquitous sense тАШalmsтАЩ and tr. it here with full desiderative sense, contra Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) тАЬein Fleischalmosen.тАЭ

+Griffith

They who observing that the Horse is ready call out and say, the smell is good; remove it;
And, craving meat, await the distribution,–may their approving help promote labour.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe stick that is dipped into the cauldron in which the flesh is boiled; the vessels that distribute the broth; the covers of the dishes, the skewers, the knives, all do honour (to the horse).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The stick: ─лk┼Ыaс╣Зam m─Бс╣Гspacany─Б ukh─Бyaс╕е;

─кk┼Ыaс╣Зam = p─Бkapar─лkс╣г─Б s─Бdhanam k─Бс╣гс╣нham, a piece of wood, an implement for testing if the cooking is effected; the vessels: p─Бtr─Бс╣Зi y┼лс╣гс╣Зa ─Бsecan─Бni = the vessels that are sprinklers of the boiled juice or broth, rasasya kvathitasya; the dishes: ┼лс╣гmaс╣Зy─Б pidh─Бn─Б, covers confining the heat;

┼кс╣гmaс╣Зy─Б = vessels for confining the heat, ┼лс╣гmaniv─Бraс╣З─Бrh─Бс╣Зi p─Бtr─Бс╣Зi;

Pidh─Бn─Б = covers of the dishes, apidh─Бn─Б car┼лс╣З─Бm;

Skewers: aс╣Еka, slips of cane, vetasa┼Ы─Бkh─Б, for marking the members of the horse as they are to be dissected. According to K─Бty─Бyana, S┼лtra 155, this is to be done by the queens, or wives of the sacrificer, and their attendants, with one hundred and one needles or skewers, which may of gold, silve,or bronze or other metal, so embellished; the knives: s┼лn─Бс╕е avad─Бna s─Бdhan─Бс╕е = implements of dissection, the svadhiti and others

+Jamison Brereton

The probe for the meat-cooking cauldron, the cups for the pouring of broth,
the covers of the bowls that keep them warm, the hooks, and the
baskets are in attendance around the horse.

The warming-pots, the covers of the dishes, hooks, carving-boards,–all these attend the Charger.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay the plural ce of going forth, of tarrying, of rolling on the ground; the foot-fastening of the horse, (the water) that he has drunk, the grass that he has eaten; may all these be thine among the gods.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

(The gear) that made him set his stride, come to a halt, and turn aside, and the foot-fetter of the steed,
and what he drank and what fodder he ateтАФlet all this of yours be also among the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The -ana-suffix on the nominals in p─Бda a marks them as transitive/causative in sense; I take these neut. singulars as referring to the tack that produce the various movements of the horse.

+Griffith

The starting-place, his place of rest and rolling, the ropes wherewith the Charger’s feet were fastened,
The water that he drank, the food he tasted,–among the Gods, too, may all these attend thee.

+Geldner

Worauf es schreitet, sich niederl├д├Яt, sich w├дlzt, und die Fu├Яfessel des Rennpferdes, was es getrunken und an Futter gefressen hat, all das soll von dir bei den G├╢ttern sein.

+Grassmann

Worauf der Renner getreten, worauf er sich gelagert und herumgew├дlzt hat, und was seines Fusses Fessel war; was er[453] getrunken, und das Futter, was er verzehrt hat, das alles sei dein eigen bei den G├╢ttern.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet not smoke-smelling Agni cause you, (horse), to utter sound; let not the glowing cauldron, odoriferous (with its contents), be overturned; the gods accept a horse that has been selected (for sacrifice); that has been led (round the fire); that has been devoutly offered, and has been consecrated by (the exclamation), vaс╣гat.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Let not: this may be addressed to the horse before the horse is killed; or, to the horse’s limbs in process of cooking, to desire them not to boil too loud, that is, too fast, lest the fire split the cauldron;

Odoriferous: jaghriс╕е tapena jighrati, smellling with heat

+Jamison Brereton

Let the fire that smells of smoke not besmirch you; let the blazing hot cauldron not topple over.
The one sacrificed, sought out, and greeted when the cry тАЬvaс╣гaс╣нтАЭ is
made: that horse do the gods receive.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

On abh├н vikta see comm. ad X.27.1.

+Griffith

Let not the fire, smoke-scented, make thee crackle, nor glowing caldron smell and break to pieces.
Offered, beloved, approved, and consecrated,–such Charger do the Gods accept with favour.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe cloth which they spread as a covering for the horse; the golden (trappings with which they decorate him), the head-ropes, the foot-ropes, all these they offer as acceptable to the gods.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

As a covering for the horse: at the time of putting the horse to death, the adh─лv─Бsa (cf. K─Бty─Бyana S┼лtra 145), a curtain is held,behind which the principal queen lies through the night by the side of the horse

+Jamison Brereton

The mantel they spread out for the horse, the over-mantel, and the gold (trappings) that are for him,
the harness, and the foot-fetterтАФ(all these), his own dear things, hold the steed fast among the gods.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The placement of ├бrvantam amid the pieces of tackle associated with him seems strange at first, but in fact it can be seen as iconic: these various items hold him, and so heтАЩs surrounded by them. ItтАЩs also clever that the various things are in the neuter, and so it is not till the verb appears (─Б╠Бy─Бmayanti at the very end of the vs.) that it becomes clear that they are the subjects of the verb and therefore nominative, while ├бrvantam is clearly accusative.

+Griffith

The robe they spread upon the Horse to clothe him, the upper covering and the golden trappings,
The halters which restrain the Steed, the heel-ropes,–all these, as grateful to the Gods, they offer.

+Geldner

Das Gewand das sie dem Pferde unterlegen, das Obergewand, die Goldsachen, die sie ihm unterlegen, die Fessel, die Fu├Яfessel, diese lieben Sachen sollen den Renner bei den G├╢ttern festhalten.

+Grassmann

Welche Decke sie ├╝ber das Pferd breiten, welcher Ueberwurf, welchen Goldschmuck, welche Halfter, welches Fussband des Rosses, all dies liebe lenken sie zu den G├╢ttern hin.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhoever has goaded you in your paces, either with heel or with whip, whilst nothing in your strength– all these (vexations) I pour out with holy prayers, as oblation with the ladle.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

If, in riding you, anyone goaded (you) with his heel or with a whip, along with too much тАЬcome on, come on,тАЭ
I make all these sweet for you with a sacred formulation, as (priests) sweeten them [=oblations?] by the ladling of the oblation at the rites.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The first hemistich is one of the few places in the RV that depicts horses being ridden (see also I.155.1, 163.2 – though for an alternative for the latter see comm. ad loc. – 163.9): both s─Бd├й lit. тАШin the seatтАЩ, here tr. тАШin ridingтАЩ, and the mention of goading with a heel require a rider physically on a horse.

I follow the general interpr. of ┼Ы┼л╠Бkс╣Ыta- as containing a syllable ┼Ы┼л╠Бused to urge on horses, hence my тАЬcome on, come on.тАЭ Although Google tells me that тАЬchirrupтАЭ and тАЬtchickтАЭ are so used (in English, or whatever we might call it), I judged that such a tr. would simply sow confusion.

The three disfavored ways of goading a horse – heel, whip, and excessive ┼Ы┼л╠Б- making – are not parallel, or rather heel and whip go together and ┼Ы┼л╠Бis something else, and they are therefore summed up with useful vagueness by s├бrv─Б t─Б╠БтАЬall theseтАЭ in d. The vagueness is also useful because none of the three is a particular suitable object for s┼лday─Бmi тАШI make sweetтАЩ, even in its most attenuated sense (Geldner тАЬтАж mache ich тАж wieder gutтАЭ).

The neut. pl. t─Б╠Бin the simile in c is more mysterious. h├бvis- тАШoblationтАЩ is a standard obj. of s┼лd├бya-, but it is coopted here by the gen. h├бviс╣гaс╕е. I have nonetheless supplied тАШoblationsтАЩ as the referent of t─Б╠Б. Geldner supplies тАЬdie FehlerтАЭ on grounds of contextual sense only. He also cites Mah. as explaining t─Б╠Бas тАЬnur F├╝llwortтАЭ – an explanation IтАЩd like to be able to use more often!

+Griffith

If one, when seated, with excessive urging hath with his heel or with his whip distressed thee,
All these thy woes, as with the oblations’ ladle at sacrifices, with my prayer I banish.

+Geldner

Wenn man dich beim Reiten durch ├╝berm├д├Яiges Hetzen oder mit der Ferse oder der Peitsche angespornt hat, all das mache ich dir mit einem Segen wieder gut, wie mit einem L├╢ffel Opferspeise die Fehler im Gottesdienst.

+Grassmann

Was bei deiner Erm├╝dung durch das Uebermass des Antreibens, oder durch die Ferse [den Sporn] oder durch die Peitsche dich gequ├дlt hat, das alles vers├╝sse ich dir durch Gebet, wie bei den Opfern durch den Butterl├╢ffel.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe axe penetrates the thirty-four ribs of the swift horse; the beloved of the gods, (the immolators), cut up (the horse) with skill, so that the limbs may be unperforated, and recapitulating joint by joint.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Thirty-four ribs: it is noted that other animals have only 24 ribs;

Unperforated: acchidr─Б g─Бtr─Б: the vi┼Ыasana kart─Бraс╕е, or dissectors, are to utter the name of the parts, as heart, tongue,breast, as they divide them; and are to so separate them that they may not have holes or perforations, they may not be mangled

+Jamison Brereton

The axe converges on the thirty-four ribs of the prizewinning horse, who has connection with the gods.
Arrange his legs, undamaged, into patterns, and carve them up joint by joint, having called them out in order.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The preverb s├бm тАШtogetherтАЩ in s├бm eti may seem an odd choice in a verse concerning cutting the horse apart. However, it sets up a contrastive pairing with v├н ┼Ыasta тАШcut apart / carve upтАЩ at the end of the 2nd hemistich, and it also anticipates (or promises) the rejoining of the parts of the horse that ends the hymn.

As it turns out, horses have 36 ribs, not 34. Max M├╝ller noted this in 1875 and got a potential explanation from T. H. Huxley – that it may be that theyтАЩre cutting the rib cartilage and they donтАЩt cut the last two ribs in order to keep the carcass together: [http://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Popular_Science_Monthly/Volume_7/June_1875/A_C urious_Question_of_Horses’_Ribs]

+Griffith

The four-and-thirty ribs of the. Swift Charger, kin to the Gods, the slayer’s hatchet pierces.
Cut ye with skill, so that the parts be flawless, and piece by piece declaring them dissect them.

+Geldner

Auf vierunddrei├Яig Rippen des g├╢ttergesellten Streitrosses trifft das Beil. Richtet die K├╢rperteile unverletzt her, zerleget sie Glied f├╝r Glied der Reihe nach ausrufend!

+Grassmann

Die vierunddreissig Rippen des gottverwandten Rosses erreicht das Beil; macht nun es kunstreich, dass jedes Glied unverletzt sei, Gelenk f├╝r Gelenk, es laut nennend, schneidet aus.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThere is one immolator of the radiant horse, which is Time; there are two that hold him fast; such of your limbs as I cut up in due season, I offer them, made into balls (of meat) upon the fire.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Time: с╣Ыtuс╕е, properly season; by metonymy, time; there are two: day and night, or heaven and earth

+Jamison Brereton

There is one carver of Tvaс╣гс╣нarтАЩs horse and two to hold him fast: such is the proper way.
The (sacrificial portions) I make from your legs according to the proper order, just those lumps, one after the other, do I offer in the fire.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

In d I didnтАЩt tr. p├нс╣Зс╕Н─Бn─Бm as a partitive gen. because the English got too fussy. Geldner thinks that the p├нс╣Зс╕Нa- are rice balls, but this seems anachronistically to reflect later ritual use of the word.

+Griffith

Of Tvastar’s Charger there is one dissector,–this is the custom-two there are who guide him.
Such of his limbs as I divide in order, these, amid the balls, in fire I offer.

+Geldner

Einer ist der Zerleger des Rosses des Tvastri, zwei sind es, die es halten. So ist das richtige Verh├дltnis. So viele deiner K├╢rperteile ich nach der Reihenfolge herrichte, so viele Kl├╢├Яe opfere ich ins Feuer.

+Grassmann

Einer ist es, der das Ross des Tvaschtar zerlegt, zwei, die es darreichen, so ist die Regel; welche deiner Glieder ich regelrecht zurichte, die St├╝cke alle opfere ich dem Agni.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet not your precious body grieve you, who are going verily (to the gods); let not the axe linger in your body; let not the greedy and unskilful (immolator) missing the members, mangle your limbs needlessly with his knife.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Let your own dear lifebreath not burn you as you go along; let the axe not bring the parts of your body to a standstill.
Let a greedy man who is no carver, skipping steps, not make your legs damaged with a knife gone awry.

+Jamison Brereton Notes

The caus. redupl. aor. ─Б╠Бtiс╣гс╣нhipat is tr. by most as тАШcause enduring painтАЩ vel sim., which is far from the lit. meaning of the lexeme. The caus. to ─Б╠БтИЪsth─Б sometimes means тАШmake stand stillтАЩ, and I think that sense is in play here. The horse is about to go on a journey (apiy├бntam тАШgoing alongтАЩ in p─Бda a; more fully described in 21b), but various mishaps can keep that journey from happening and make the horse stop.

+Griffith

Let not thy dear soul burn thee as thou comest, let not the hatchet linger in thy body.
Let not a greedy clumsy immolator, missing the joints, mangle thy limbs unduly.

+Geldner

Nicht soll dich das liebe Leben schmerzen, wenn du eingehst; nicht soll das Beil deinem K├╢rper dauernden Schaden tun. Nicht soll ein gieriger, unerfahrener Zerleger mit dem Hackmesser ausgleitend die zerschnittenen Glieder falsch behandeln.

+Grassmann

Nicht qu├дle dich der liebe Lebenshauch, wenn du [zu den G├╢ttern] eingehst, nicht thue das Beil deinen Gliedern Schaden; nicht m├╢ge dir ein hastiger, schlechter Zerleger, unrichtig verfahrend, die Glieder auf verkehrte Art zerspalten.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬVerily at this moment you do not die; nor are you harmed; for you go by auspicious paths to the gods. The horses of Indra, the steeds of the Maruts shall be yoked (to their ears), and a courser shall be plural ced in the shaft of the ass of the A┼Ыvins (to bear you to heaven).тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Truly in this way you do not die nor are you harmed: you go to the gods by paths easy to travel.
The two fallow bays (of Indra) and the two dappled mares (of the
Maruts) have become your yokemates. The prizewinning (horse) has taken his place at the chariot-pole of the (A┼ЫvinsтАЩ) donkey.

+Griffith

No, here thou diest not, thou art not injured: by easy paths unto the Gods thou goest.
Both Bays, both spotted mares are now thy fellows, and to the ass’s pole is yoked the Charger.

+Geldner

Wahrlich, nicht stirbst du dabei, nicht nimmst du Schaden. Zu den G├╢ttern gehst du auf gangbaren Wegen. Die beiden Falben, die beiden Schecken sind deine Jochgenossen geworden; das Streitro├Я ward an die Deichsel des Esels eingestellt.

+Grassmann

F├╝rwahr nicht stirbst du hier, nicht leidest du Schaden; nein, zu den G├╢ttern gehst du auf sch├╢ngebahnten Pfaden; die beiden goldfarbnen Rosse [des Indra], die weissgefleckten Gazellen [der Maruts] sind deine Genossen geworden; an des Eselhengstes Deichsel hat sich das schnelle Ross gestellt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬMay this horse bring to us all-sustaining wealth, with abundance of cows of excellent horses, and of male offspring; may the spirited steed bring us exemption from wickedness; may this horse, offered in oblation, procure for us bodily vigour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The spirited steed;

Aditi = not poor or mean, ad─лna, as an epithet of a┼Ыva

+Jamison Brereton

(Let) the prizewinner (win) for us a mass of good cattle and good horses, male children, and all-prospering wealth.
Let Aditi make guiltlessness for us. Let the horse, accompanied by our oblations, win sovereignty for us.

+Griffith

May this Steed bring us all-sustaining riches, wealth in good kine, good horses, manly offspring.
Freedom from sin may Aditi vouchsafe us: the Steed with our oblations gain us lordship!

+Geldner

Sch├╢ne Rinder und sch├╢ne Rosse, m├дnnliche Kinder und alln├дhrenden Besitz soll uns das siegesgewohnte Ro├Я bringen. Schuldlosigkeit soll uns Aditi erwirken. Die Herrschaft soll uns das von Opfergaben begleitete Ro├Я erringen!

+Grassmann

Reichthum an Rindern und Rossen schaffe uns das Ross, Helden und S├╢hne und alln├дhrenden Reichthum; Aditi schaffe uns Schuldlosigkeit, und das opferreiche Pferd verleihe uns Herrschaft.

+Elizarenkova
